ENTRY            20157   20190112                             227320157  0    1 
SUBENT        20157001   20190112                             227320157  1    1 
BIB                 16         71                                 20157  1    2 
TITLE       Elastic neutron scattering from Ca-40 for neutron     20157  1    3 
            energies to 2 MeV                                     20157  1    4 
AUTHOR     (J.Nebe, G.J.Kirouac)                                  20157  1    5 
INSTITUTE  (2GERKFK)                                              20157  1    6 
REFERENCE  (J,NP/A,185,113,1972)  Final paper.                    20157  1    7 
           (W,NEBE,197012)        Cross-section data on cards.    20157  1    8 
           (J,NP/A,154,36,1970)  spin and l-values, partly suprsdd20157  1    9 
           (R,KFK-1069,1,1969) - prelim results                   20157  1   10 
REL-REF    (R,20010006,J.Nebe+,R,KFK-1000,1968) Total cross-sect. 20157  1   11 
           (I,,S.Cierjacks+,J,RSI,39,1279,1968)   Experim.details 20157  1   12 
FACILITY   (ISOCY,2GERKFK) Karlsruhe isochronous cyclotron (KIC)  20157  1   13 
INC-SOURCE .U-(d,nx) reaction by 40 MeV deuterons.                20157  1   14 
            A deflection system produced neutron bunches of about 20157  1   15 
            1 ns duration at a repetition rate of 19.13 kHz,      20157  1   16 
            neutron flux about 3.e+4 n/cm2*sec.  The neutron beam 20157  1   17 
            was monitored by a pulse-shape discriminator detector.20157  1   18 
INC-SPECT  .The neutron spectrum from the Karlsruhe isochronous   20157  1   19 
            cyclotron spectrometer is a smooth, slowly varying    20157  1   20 
            function in the energy region from 0.55 to 2 MeV.     20157  1   21 
SAMPLE     .A metallic calcium cylinder, 5 cm diameter            20157  1   22 
            and 12 cm long, encapsulated in 50 mu silver foil,    20157  1   23 
            the thickness = 0.09 atoms/barns.                     20157  1   24 
           .The sample purity better than 99.5%.                  20157  1   25 
           .For normalization to the scattering cross section, a  20157  1   26 
            high purity (99.9%) graphite sample was used in the   20157  1   27 
            form of a hollow cylinder with an inner diam. of 2.5cm20157  1   28 
            and the same outer dimensions as calcium sample.      20157  1   29 
METHOD     (TOF)    Flight path = 58 m, overall time resolution   20157  1   30 
            is 4 ns. (i.e. energy resolution of 700 eV at 0.55 MeV20157  1   31 
            and 6.1 keV at 2 MeV).                                20157  1   32 
DETECTOR   (SCIN)    Three NE-102A plastic scintillators, 12.4 cm 20157  1   33 
            diameter by 2.5 cm thick, mounted on XP-1040          20157  1   34 
            photo-multipliers, and fast anode output had a zero   20157  1   35 
            crossover tunnel diode time mark circuit.             20157  1   36 
           .As the neutron flux detector, a small NE-102A         20157  1   37 
            scintillator (5 cm diameter, 1.2 cm thick) was used.  20157  1   38 
           .The system (4 NE-102A detectors, a detector position  20157  1   39 
            coder and Laben UC-KB time analyser) coupled to a     20157  1   40 
            CDC-3100 on-line computer.                            20157  1   41 
           .The TOF spectrum for each detector was taken over a   20157  1   42 
            range of 4 microsec with channel widths of 2ns.       20157  1   43 
           .A neutron beam monitor placed at 6 deg to the neutron 20157  1   44 
            beam at a distance of 11 m from the source.           20157  1   45 
           .By aluminum collimator, 30 cm in diameter by 1 m long,20157  1   46 
            the neutron beam confined to 3.0 micro-steradian at   20157  1   47 
            the end of the 58 m flight path.                      20157  1   48 
           .Data were simultaneously taken at laboratory angles of20157  1   49 
            54, 90 and 140 degrees by 3 scattering detectors, and 20157  1   50 
            0 deg for flux monitoring (NE-102A).                  20157  1   51 
MONITOR    (6-C-12(N,EL)6-C-12,,DA)                               20157  1   52 
MONIT-REF  (,A.Langsdorf+,J,PR,107,1077,1957)                     20157  1   53 
CORRECTION .Corrections were made for the finite scattering sample20157  1   54 
            thickness of Ca and C measured with similar energy    20157  1   55 
            resolution at the KIC spectrometer, in the calculation20157  1   56 
            of the cross section.  The correction was small for   20157  1   57 
            thin Ca sample but was about 20% for C data,          20157  1   58 
            no corrections were made for multiple scattering.     20157  1   59 
           .Back ground counting rates in the open beam spectrum  20157  1   60 
            were less than 5% of the sample out counting          20157  1   61 
            rate above 1 MeV. Below this energy the fraction      20157  1   62 
            increased to 15%.                                     20157  1   63 
COMMENT    .The primary purpose of the work was to assign spins   20157  1   64 
            and parities (l-values) for Ca40(n,n) resonances by   20157  1   65 
            the resonance shapes and symmetry properties.  Precise20157  1   66 
            absolute values for the Ca-40 differential scattering 20157  1   67 
            cross section were not the principal concern.         20157  1   68 
HISTORY    (19701204C)                                            20157  1   69 
           (19720512A)  n-widths, aver. Res. Pars added.          20157  1   70 
           (20190112U) SD:Updated to new date formats,lower case. 20157  1   71 
           BIB updated. ERR-ANALYS moved to Subents 002-004.      20157  1   72 
           REL-REF added.                                         20157  1   73

REACTION   (20-CA-40(N,EL)20-CA-40,,DA)                           20157  2    3 
COMMENT    .The differential neutron scattering cross section from20157  2    4 
            0.55 to 2.0 MeV is given with high energy resolution, 20157  2    5 
            the first inelastic channel opens at 3.35 MeV. For a  20157  2    6 
            lower threshold (200 keV neutrons) of the detector    20157  2    7 
            and a short sample-detector distance (24.4 cm),       20157  2    8 
            inelastically scattered neutrons are not detected.    20157  2    9 
REL-REF    (A,10415013,R.O.Lane+,J,AP,12,135,1961)  The data agree20157  2   10 
            well but direct comparison is difficult because of the20157  2   11 
            widely different resolution functions.                20157  2   12 
ERR-ANALYS (ERR-S) The statistical error is given as 3% and       20157  2   13 
           (ERR-T,,15.) after normalizing to the carbon, the      20157  2   14 
           absolute cross section values are estimated to  have   20157  2   15 
           less than 15% uncertainty.                             20157  2   16

REACTION   (20-CA-40(N,0),,L)                                     20157 10    3 
ANALYSIS   .R-matrix formalism is applied and formula by Blatt and20157 10    4 
            Biedenharn are used to calculating the angular        20157 10    5 
            dependence of scattering and reaction processes.      20157 10    6 
           .The method of shape identification used here requires 20157 10    7 
            some knowledge of the background scattering (i.e.     20157 10    8 
            channel radius and potential scattering).             20157 10    9 
           .the assignments of resonance spin and parity have     20157 10   10 
            utilized 3 general features of the differential cross-20157 10   11 
            section such as,(1) the resonance shape, (2) the      20157 10   12 
            amplitude behavior as function of scattering angle,   20157 10   13 
            (3) the peak position shift.                          20157 10   14 
           .The angular momentum l is based on the shape analysis 20157 10   15 
            of differential cross section and on the total cross  20157 10   16 
            section results of KFK-1000.                          20157 10   17 
           .parity = (-)**l.                                      20157 10   18 
FLAG       (1.)       Taken from nucl.Phys.,A154(1970)36.         20157 10   19

           (3.)       Uncertain, l=1 also possible.               20157 10   21
